  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_e138551a-efc5-456b-b764-5dbe5fa02b30'
      });

<span id="freeTextContainer13195732111511440115">Stephen King returns to the characters and territory of one of his most popular novels ever, The Shining, in this instantly riveting novel about the now middle-aged Dan Torrance (the boy protagonist of The Shining) and the very special 12-year-old girl he must save from a tribe of murderous paranormals.<br/><br/>On highways across America, a tribe of people called The True Knot trav</span>
  <span id="freeText13195732111511440115" style="display:none">Stephen King returns to the characters and territory of one of his most popular novels ever, The Shining, in this instantly riveting novel about the now middle-aged Dan Torrance (the boy protagonist of The Shining) and the very special 12-year-old girl he must save from a tribe of murderous paranormals.<br /><br />On highways across America, a tribe of people called The True Knot travel in search of sustenance. They look harmless - mostly old, lots of polyester, and married to their RVs. But as Dan Torrance knows, and spunky 12-year-old Abra Stone learns, The True Knot are quasi-immortal, living off the "steam" that children with the "shining" produce when they are slowly tortured to death.<br /><br />Haunted by the inhabitants of the Overlook Hotel where he spent one horrific childhood year, Dan has been drifting for decades, desperate to shed his father's legacy of despair, alcoholism, and violence. Finally, he settles in a New Hampshire town, an AA community that sustains him, and a job at a nursing home where his remnant "shining" power provides the crucial final comfort to the dying. Aided by a prescient cat, he becomes "Doctor Sleep."<br /><br />Then Dan meets the evanescent Abra Stone, and it is her spectacular gift, the brightest shining ever seen, that reignites Dan's own demons and summons him to a battle for Abra's soul and survival. This is an epic war between good and evil, a gory, glorious story that will thrill the millions of hyper-devoted fans of The Shining and wildly satisfy anyone new to the territory of this icon in the King canon.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13195732111511440115" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      </div>
</div>

<a href="/questions/430610-i-didn-t-read-the-shining-but-in-the">I didn&#39;t read the &quot;Shining,&quot; but in the movie, Dick Hallorann is attacked by Jack Torrance&#39;s wielding ax, and I presumed he died...Does he survive in the book?</a>
</div>
<div class='communityQAFooter questionFooter'>
<ul class='questionFooterActions'>

<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_430610'><a id="like_count_community_question_430610" rel="nofollow" href="/rating/voters/430610?resource_type=CommunityQuestion"><span class="likesCount">19 likes</span></a>&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F16130549-doctor-sleep">like</a></span>

<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/11975160-xepherus3"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1545101247i/11975160._UX100_CR0,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/11975160-xepherus3">Xepherus3</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">Please do not use the Shining movie as your reference to the story of the Torrances. The movie took extreme liberties with King's printed word. And af<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">Please do not use the Shining movie as your reference to the story of the Torrances. The movie took extreme liberties with King's printed word. And after reading the book, I was disappointed with the film. Dick Hallorann is alive and well at the end of the Shining novel, and is a great part of Doctor Sleep. Kubrick's film is great on it's own, but the book crushes that screenplay into dust.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>

<div id="review_488188302" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/488188302" />
    <a title="Greg" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/359659-greg"><img alt="Greg" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1304087397p2/359659.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/488188302?book_show_action=true">Dec 28, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Greg" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Greg" href="/user/show/359659-greg">Greg</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781451698848" href="/book/show/15800656-doctor-sleep">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer488188302" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8639977056393370595">(Disclosure: I used to work at Stephen King's publisher and read <i>Doctor Sleep</i> in December 2012.) <br/><br/>Get ready. If I can make just one recommendation: whether you're a longtime King fan or fairly new to his stuff, it wouldn't be the worst thing to read <i>The Shining</i> before you get your hands on <i>Doctor Sleep</i>. Seasoned fans know that the movie, while engrossing in its own right, is very different in many ways, and doesn't even begin to plumb the psychological depths that the book does. You could read an</span>
  <span id="freeText8639977056393370595" style="display:none">(Disclosure: I used to work at Stephen King's publisher and read <i>Doctor Sleep</i> in December 2012.) <br /><br />Get ready. If I can make just one recommendation: whether you're a longtime King fan or fairly new to his stuff, it wouldn't be the worst thing to read <i>The Shining</i> before you get your hands on <i>Doctor Sleep</i>. Seasoned fans know that the movie, while engrossing in its own right, is very different in many ways, and doesn't even begin to plumb the psychological depths that the book does. You could read and love <i>Doctor Sleep</i> without doing so, but I think people's experiences of this sequel will only be enriched by first checking out one of the mothers of all horror novels. </span>
  <a data-text-id="8639977056393370595" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_722776722" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/722776722" />
    <a title="Will Byrnes" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1526851-will-byrnes"><img alt="Will Byrnes" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1291462190p2/1526851.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/722776722?book_show_action=true">Sep 18, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Will Byrnes" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Will Byrnes" href="/user/show/1526851-will-byrnes">Will Byrnes</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1526851-will-byrnes?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1526851-will-byrnes?shelf=stephen-king">stephen-king</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1526851-will-byrnes?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1526851-will-byrnes?shelf=horror">horror</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer722776722" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18260842963918192628">There is a boy (now a man) a girl, a band of baddies with a charismatic leader, a coalition of the willing, battles to be fought, supernatural elements and magical powers. Stephen King was at this long before Harry Potter lived under the stairs. He has a preternatural (not to say supernatural) talent for writing kids, and can keep you turning pages, losing sleep, and getting back late to work from your lunch breaks. <br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380867454i/3139396.jpg' width='400' height='550' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><i>from King’s site</i> <br/><br/>We will presume for the purposes of this review that you have r</span>
  <span id="freeText18260842963918192628" style="display:none">There is a boy (now a man) a girl, a band of baddies with a charismatic leader, a coalition of the willing, battles to be fought, supernatural elements and magical powers. Stephen King was at this long before Harry Potter lived under the stairs. He has a preternatural (not to say supernatural) talent for writing kids, and can keep you turning pages, losing sleep, and getting back late to work from your lunch breaks. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380867454i/3139396.jpg" width="400" height="550" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>from King’s site</i> <br><br>We will presume for the purposes of this review that you have read, or at least seen one version of <i>The Shining</i>. If you have not, read no further, as there are details here that would be considered spoilerish were they to appear in a review of that book. And if you have not read <i>The Shining</i> you should probably do so before taking on <i>Doctor Sleep</i>, a sequel. Ok, everyone here has read <i>The Shining</i>, yes? All right, but we are using the honor system here, and do not want to ruin the fun of reading that one for anyone. So, as long as you’re sure…<br><br>At the end of <i>The Shining</i>, three people survive the carnage, Danny Torrance, a five year old with a special gift, Wendy Torrance, Danny’s mother and newly widowed wife of the late Jack Torrance, and Dick Halloran, an employee of The Overlook and possessor of a gift like Danny’s, one that allowed him to hear Danny’s psychic 911 call and return from his home in Florida in time to do something about it. What happened next? <br><br>King does not typically do sequels, if one does not count books that are part of a planned series, but<blockquote> Every now and then somebody would ask, ‘Whatever happened to Danny?’ I used to joke around and say, ‘He married Charlie McGee from <i>Firestarter</i> and they had these amazing kids!’ But I did sort of wonder about it. – (from <a href="http://shelf-life.ew.com/2013/02/01/stephen-king-the-shining-doctor-sleep-preview/" rel="nofollow noopener">EW</a>)</blockquote>One of the central features of <i>The Shining</i> was Jack’s Torrance’s battle with alcoholism. As with the real world, King’s fictional realm notes that alcoholism runs in families. And one of the criticisms of <i>The Shining</i> was that the possibility of Jack considering getting some help from AA is never even raised. If King has ever considered that to have been an oversight, I have not seen that interview. But it is clear that he has given the matter some thought.<blockquote> Jack Torrance never tries Alcoholics Anonymous. That is never even mentioned in "The Shining." He has what they call white-knuckle sobriety. He's doing it all by himself. So, I wondered what it would be like to see Danny first as an alcoholic, and then see him in AA. (from an <a href="http://www.npr.org/2013/09/24/223105565/stephen-king-on-getting-scared-nothing-like-your-first-time" rel="nofollow noopener">NPR Interview</a>)</blockquote><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1573190538i/28419421._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="xxx" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>Ewan McGregor</b> as Danny Torrance in the film<br><br>It gives nothing away to let you know that Danny is a true Torrance. Not only does he self-medicate to quiet the terrors that still haunt him, he is far from the best person he can be.<blockquote>I knew if I did this sequel I’d have to try to put together some of the same elements, but at the same time I didn’t want to make it too similar. I didn’t want to make Danny a grown up with kids of his own, and try to replicate that whole losing-your-temper-because-you’re-drunk thing. But I did think to myself: ‘Not only alcoholism can be a family disease, but rage can be a family disease.’ You find that the guys who abuse their children were abused themselves as kids. That certainly fit Danny as I knew him. – from <a href="http://shelf-life.ew.com/2013/02/01/stephen-king-the-shining-doctor-sleep-preview/" rel="nofollow noopener">EW</a>
</blockquote>All SK novels require a baddie, or a set of them. No disappointment here. King has again succeeded in taking the ordinary and making it horrifying.<blockquote>Driving back and forth from Maine to Florida, which I do twice a year, I’m always seeing all these recreational vehicles — the bounders in the Winnebagos. I always think to myself, ‘Who is in those things?’ You pass them a thousand times at rest stops. They’re always the ones wearing the shirts that say ‘God Does Not Deduct From a Lifespan Time Spent Fishing.’ They’re always lined up at the McDonald’s, slowing the whole line down. And I always thought to myself, ‘There’s something really sinister about those people because they’re so unobtrusive, yet so pervasive.’ I just wanted to use that. It would be the perfect way to travel around America and be unobtrusive if you were really some sort of awful creature. – from <a href="http://shelf-life.ew.com/2013/02/01/stephen-king-the-shining-doctor-sleep-preview/" rel="nofollow noopener">EW</a>
</blockquote>This wandering band call themselves <i>The True Knot</i>. They feed on the essence of those gifted with the sort of talent people like Danny possess. It provides them with extraordinary longevity, but as with their Transylvanian counterparts, the need is ongoing and the supply is limited. Like right-wing politicians they are more than happy to gorge on the pain of others and are shown here feasting on the spirits set adrift on 9/11. The usual condiments for this substance they call <i>steam</i> will not do. The taste and benefit is enhanced, however, if their victims endure extreme and prolonged torture. Does Ted Cruz drive a Winnebago? King gives the members Damon Runyon-esque names, like Crow Daddy, Steamboat Steve and Tommy the Truck.<br><br>By the time you finish reading <i>Doctor Sleep</i> you might have a new image of the top hat to consider next time you are planning a formal night out. We all have one, probably this one:<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380867454i/3139397.jpg" width="400" height="xxx" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>But the baddie in Stephen King’s latest is likely to do for the top hat what this guy<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380867454i/3139398._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="260" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>did for the derby. Rose O’Hara, the leader of a group called The True Knot, won’t leave home without it. It adds a nice visual element, calling to mind a certain <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Baron_Samedi" rel="nofollow noopener">Caribbean Baron</a>, and making Rosie even more riveting. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1573190707i/28419435._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="xxx" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>Rebecca Ferguson</b> as Rose the Hat- from the film<br><br>And what of our young heroine? Abra is born with a shining of prodigious proportions. (btw, the name Abra was inspired by Abra Bacon, a character in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/4406.East_of_Eden" rel="nofollow noopener">East of Eden</a>) She manages to send out a signal even when she is newly arrived. She’s a good kid, despite scaring her parents on occasion with tricks like making all the silverware in the kitchen take to the air, or causing the odd earthquake when she does a mental <a href="http://marvel.wikia.com/wiki/Bruce_Banner_(Earth-616)" rel="nofollow noopener">Bruce</a> (or if you prefer, <a href="http://hulk.wikia.com/wiki/David_Banner" rel="nofollow noopener">David</a>) Banner. Don’t make her angry. You wouldn’t like her when she’s angry. Bad-ass teen girl power fuh shoo-uh. But, just as Danny needed Dick Hallorann and Tony, Abra needs help as well. That she and Danny will team up is a foregone conclusion. <br><br>As for Danny, the shining never left him, despite his attempts to wipe it out with spirits of a different sort. But he finds the help <i>he</i> needs and manages to put his talent to good use. He works in a hospice, the Helen Rivington House, in Frazier, NH, easing the transition for those near death, with the assistance of a resident feline, and earning himself the name <i>Doctor Sleep</i>, which also serves to remind us of what his parents called him.<blockquote>…It is this moment of transition that Doctor Sleep deals with and the idea, like so many of King's, came from an incidental story in a newspaper. This one was about "a cat in a hospice that knows when people are going to die. He would go into that patient's room and curl up next to them. And I thought, that's a good advertisement for death, for the emissary of death. I thought, 'I can make Dan the human equivalent of that cat, and call him Doctor Sleep.' There was the book." – from an interview in <a href="http://www.theguardian.com/books/2013/sep/21/stephen-king-shining-sequel-interview" rel="nofollow noopener">The Guardian</a>
</blockquote>King has a bit of fun, naming the cat Azzie, short for Azreel, the archangel of death. Cute. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1573192408i/28419483._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="xxx" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>Azzie</b> - the real Doctor Sleep - image from TheReelBits.com<br><br>What else do you need, really? Dark vs light, colorful baddies vs our everyman and everygirl. And that is indeed enough. But it is not all that King uses. He gives us a look at how people can really help people overcome, or at least handle their problems. When asked, in the NPR interview, whether his AA depictions were from personal experience, King says that the second part of AA stands for Anonymous, so he declined to offer a yes or no, however<blockquote> You could say, having read these two books and knowing that I was a very heavy drinker at the time that I wrote "The Shining," and I haven't had a drink in about 25 years now - you could draw certain conclusions from that…I've done a lot of personal research in these subjects. - from <a href="http://www.npr.org/2013/09/24/223105565/stephen-king-on-getting-scared-nothing-like-your-first-time" rel="nofollow noopener">NPR interview</a>
</blockquote>AA figures very large in this story, is central really. And the wisdom one can find in AA permeates the novel, from the importance of recognizing that we need help from others, to accepting our past and dealing with it, a very strong, serious element. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1573191122i/28419450._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="xxx" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>Kyleigh Curran</b> as Abra Stone - image from the gww.com<br><br>King sets the time of the events by referring to external realities, like who the president is, calls on contemporary cultural references, such as a mention of the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sons_of_Anarchy" rel="nofollow noopener"> Sons of Anarchy</a> and a Hank Wiliams Jr song. He also mentions a variety of other writers in his travels, some approvingly, (John Sandford, George Seferis, Bernard Malamud, Bill Wilson) some not so much (the authors of the <i>Twilight</i> and <i>Hunger Games</i> series, and Dean Koontz and Lisa Gardner, although he may merely be playing with the latter two). He also drops in an Easter egg reference to <i>Salem’s Lot</i> and make two references (that I caught anyway) to his son, Joe’s, imagined world from Joe’s book, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/483336047" target="”_blank”" rel="nofollow noopener">NOS4A2</a>.<br> <br>It has been my experience with reading Stephen King that his conclusions sometimes offer a poor partner to the journey one takes in reaching them. That is much less the case here. The ending is not an alien spider disguised as Tim Curry with bad fashion sense or alien young playing with humans in a ham-fisted manner. And the journey is indeed fun. But I had some gripes. King gives Dick Hallorann a cameo here, which was fine, and the strongest of those. Tony returns for a look-see but goes alarmingly quiet at crucial moments. We could have used a lot more about Tony other than the weak explanation that is offered near the end. If the True Knot are so bad-ass, how come there are so few of them? There is an explanation offered of prey-predator stability of numbers, but I found that unpersuasive. And why the hell introduce <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Jack if he is not going to be a part of the action?  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> This is one that actively irked. <br><br>Sequels present a danger. One of the things that is stimulating about any book, any story is newness. That is why most sequels are not as popular as their predecessors. It is hard to avoid a been-there-done-that problem when working atop existing material. The next story in line is unlikely to retain the sparkle, the shine of what went before. Given the constraints, <i>Doctor Sleep</i> fares better than most as a follow-on. There is enough distance in the story from the events of the past, and little enough overlap with those characters that the story seems fresh. When events from <i>The Shining</i> are mentioned, they do inform the current action and do not distract much. In fact there could have been more of that. So, in that way, this is a very nice addition. There is another element involved. Any event, any activity, is a product of the thing itself and of the perspective from which we view or participate in it. I read <i>The Shining</i> many years ago. I was an adult then, in my late twenties, and remember it as a VERY SCARY story. I have not come across much in horror lit that is still scary in that way, in the several decades since. I will not have any nights (on in my case days) of lost sleep because of the images King has proferred. But then, I am getting on, and am looking at those scary things with aging eyes. Someone younger (which would be almost all of you reading this) might find them far more frightening than I did. <br><br>So while <i>Doctor Sleep</i> might not cause much by way of lost rest, it is good, mainstream Stephen King and thus, hardly a snooze. The Doctor of Horror is in. Wake up!<br><br>Posted October 4, 2013<br><br>The film was released November 8, 2019<br><br>This review is cross-posted at <a href="http://cootsreviews.com/2013/10/04/doctor-sleep-by-stephen-king/" rel="nofollow noopener">Coot's Reviews</a><br><br><br>=======In the summer of 2019 GR reduced the allowable review size by 25%. As a result it was necessary to export the EXTRA STUFF to Comment #5 below</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_727063206" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/727063206" />
    <a title="Kemper" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/405390-kemper"><img alt="Kemper" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1495476851p2/405390.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/727063206?book_show_action=true">Sep 24, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kemper" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kemper" href="/user/show/405390-kemper">Kemper</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/405390-kemper?shelf=uncle-stevie">uncle-stevie</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/405390-kemper?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/405390-kemper?shelf=spooky-powers">spooky-powers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/405390-kemper?shelf=2013">2013</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer727063206" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3222311054376043253">Remember that psychic little kid in <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/6595533' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Shining</a>? Have you ever wondered what he’d be like as an adult after surviving a haunted hotel that drove his drunken father crazy and gave him a case of the redrums? If so, you’re in luck because Stephen King has now told us what happened to Danny Torrance, and he’s just as screwed up from his experience as you’d expect him to be.<br/><br/>Like his father, Dan has grown up to be a bad tempered drunk, and he uses the booze to blot out his psychic powers as he drifts </span>
  <span id="freeText3222311054376043253" style="display:none">Remember that psychic little kid in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/6595533" rel="nofollow noopener">The Shining</a>? Have you ever wondered what he’d be like as an adult after surviving a haunted hotel that drove his drunken father crazy and gave him a case of the redrums? If so, you’re in luck because Stephen King has now told us what happened to Danny Torrance, and he’s just as screwed up from his experience as you’d expect him to be.<br /><br />Like his father, Dan has grown up to be a bad tempered drunk, and he uses the booze to blot out his psychic powers as he drifts from town to town working menial jobs. The early part of the book focuses on Dan hitting bottom, and then trying to pull himself together with the help of Alcoholics Anonymous. He winds up with a job as an orderly at a hospice where he earns the nickname of Doctor Sleep for his ability to provide an easier death for the patients. <br /><br />Dan becomes aware of a little girl named Abra with a shining ability that dwarfs his own, but unfortunately Abra has also come to the attention of group of vampire like creatures calling themselves the True Knot. They pretend to be humans who roam the country as a harmless pack of tourists in RVs while they track down and feed on the psychic energy collected from torturing children with the shining, and Abra would be like an all-you-can-eat buffet to them. <br /><br />This book is almost two separate stories. One is about Dan Torrance struggling to come to terms with the legacy of his father, his abilities and his alcoholism. The other is about the battle to save a little girl from a pack of vicious monsters. King does a decent job of trying to make these two tales intersect while revisiting some elements from <i>The Shining</i>, but it ends up feeling like less than the sum of its parts. Frankly, I was far more interested in Dan’s battle with the bottle than another Stephen King story about a child in danger from a supernatural threat.<br /><br />It’s not that Abra vs. the True Knot is bad. There’s a lot of genuinely creepy dread to be mined from a pack of psychic vampires roaming the country while posing as harmless middle aged farts, and King knows how to milk every drop out of that concept. And I liked the character of Abra a lot. The idea of a powerfully psychic young girl with a bit of a mean streak was great. Kinda like if Carrie White would have had decent parents and a happy childhood.<br /><br />In fact, Abra’s a little bit too powerful because she seems fully capable of kicking ass even during her first encounter with the True Knot. So while there’s a lot of nice build-up, most of what happens seems anti-climatic. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Abra and Dan pretty much settle the True Knot’s hash with only minor injuries to a supporting character and no real lasting damage. That just seems weird in a Stephen King novel which generally feature wholesale carnage and a lot more collateral damage from the bad guys. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Plus, while there’s some callbacks to <i>The Shining</i>, they mostly feel tacked on, as if King had this basic idea and then figured out ways to work in Dan’s history where he could. It’s not really organic and doesn’t seem necessary. I also think there’s a gaping plot hole in the True Knot’s key motivation to grab Abra and their scheme. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Supposedly the TKs have been around for a very long time, and yet it’s the measles they get from taking the steam from a kid that sickens them so that they think they need Abra because she’s been vaccinated. So in all their years of kid killing, including back in olden days of yore, they never snatched a kid with measles or chicken pox or polio or typhoid or something? And somehow all the children they’ve taken in modern times weren’t vaccinated against measles? None of this made a lot of sense to me. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />One word of warning for those who have only seen the movie and not read the book, King is basing this on his version, not the film and there a couple of significant differences. (I got a laugh that King couldn’t resist taking yet another shot at the Kubrick adaptation in the author’s note afterwards. I don’t think he’s ever getting over his dislike of the movie.) Also, I listened to the audio version of this, and the narration by Will Patton is simply outstanding.<br /> <br />I feared the idea of King returning to one of his best known works, but it turned out to be a remarkably solid effort with a lot of things I liked about it. I only wish that that I’d have found the rest of the book as compelling as finding out what kind of man the kid from the Overlook Hotel grew up to be.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3222311054376043253" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1431525361" />
    <a title="megs_bookrack" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/48328025-megs-bookrack"><img alt="megs_bookrack" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1532027727p2/48328025.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1431525361?book_show_action=true">Nov 02, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="megs_bookrack" class="user" itemprop="url" name="megs_bookrack" href="/user/show/48328025-megs-bookrack">megs_bookrack</a>
      </span>

        rated it

He's also trying to get sober. What I found in reading the book is that not only did Dan inherit the alcoholism from his father, he started drinking to stop the shining and the bad things it put in his head. But, from time to time his friend Dick's words would come back to him.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1455381176i/18095639.jpg" alt=" : " class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>---&gt;EXCERPTS&lt;---</b><br><br><b>
  <blockquote>It will never stop, Danny thought. The Overlook burned and the most terrible revenants went into the lockboxes, but I can't lock away the shining, because it isn't just inside me, it is me. Without booze to at least stun it, these visions will go on until they drive me insane.<br><br>Then, like a flashlight beam in the dark, Hallorann's voice: Son, you may see things, but they're like pictures in a book. You weren't helpless in the Overlook when you were a child, and you're not helpless now. Far from it. Close your eyes and when you open them, all this crap will be gone.</blockquote>
</b><br><br>So Danny now Dan lives in the town of Frazier and is a groundskeeper for a little village called Teeny Town. He works with a man that turns out to be a good friend and fellow shiner named Billy Freeman. Billy doesn't have the shining as strong as Dan but it's still there. He gets him the job and the man that runs most of the town gets Dan in AA and it's all going good. <br><br>Meanwhile, down the way little Abra Stone is born and she is born with a powerful shining. I just love her. She starts contacting Dan when she gets a little older. They are more connected than they know at first, but I'm not telling you what that is :-) <br><br>A little bit later Dan starts working at Rivington House, it's an elderly home and he helps them when they are going to pass over. He's so very kind to these people and I love this about him. <br><br>Then.... there are these evil bastards that call themselves the True Knot. They have been around for years, they pray on the deaths of kids with the shining. They suck in their steam. Yeah, it's a little crazy but I like this story line. I don't like these people and couldn't wait to see them strung up in their own knot. They also go to major disasters and stand around sucking in the steam of what I'm guessing anyone with the shining in them that were in the disaster. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1455381176i/18095640.jpg" alt=" : " class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>They have a leader that is the most evil of them all and she's coming after Abra. Beware Rosie the Hat, until she meets her match! <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1455381176i/18095641.jpg" alt=" : " class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I loved this book so much. Just to be taken back into the world of The Shining, I know it's not the same, but to have a book that continued The Shining was so wonderful. It turned out that the True Knot owned a campground that was set up where the Overlook used to be, that opened up a whole new can of worms. There IS something that happened there that brought a tear to my eye :-( <br><br> I wish this one was a movie too!!<br><br>Mel 🖤🐶🐺🐾</span>

  <span id="freeText17938006233776362898" style="display:none">SEVEN THINGS FLASHING IN MY MIND when somebody asks me “ did you watch Shining?”<br />One : The car moves along the road and we see the humongous mountains and Wendy Carlos and Rachel Elkind’s eerie composition starts to play on the images as we whirl around the mountains…<br /><br />TWO: Grady Twins’ spooky images as we see them stand up holding hands near open door! They say in unison: “Come, play with us Danny!” (This year I told my husband their clothes could be best pair for our Halloween costumes. And he blurted out his beer on my face. What a jerk! But he surprised me to buy tickets to Overlook Hotel for one night. I imminently forgave him even he made the reservation for one and he bought me only one way ticket! He really loves me so much J))<br /><br />THREE: Little Danny Torrence’s screams as he keeps replying the same haunted words: “REDRUM! REDRUM! REDRUM!”<br /><br />FOUR: At room 237:Jack thinks he kisses a young, sexy woman, appears naked behind the shower curtains. But he accidentally takes a look their kissing reflection in the mirror, he finds out he’s kissing an old woman whose shaggy body is covered in scars. He begins to run away (Actually I laughed at this scene so much! Cheater Jack couldn’t get away with his two minutes stand !!!)<br /><br />FIVE: JACK’S NEW NOVEL COMING UP RELEASING SOON: “All work no play!”: Revelation scene Wendy finds out Jack has written the same words over and over again and turned into “DULL BOY!” was memorable and one of the creepier parts of the story!<br /><br />SIX: Here’s Jackkk!!! He finally loses the rest of his marbles, swinging an axe, breaking a door and screaming Johnny Carson’s famous theme in version!<br /><br />And SEVEN: We see Jack trapped in the maze, froze to death, scariest, epic expression on his face (scary and sarcastically awkward, just a little bit. I know I’m the weird one who is thrown away from the theaters for laughing too much at the horror movies!)<br /><br />I know I didn’t talk about the book. I talked about the epic, scaring you shameless (or sh**tless) scenes of the movie. But even MY KING says the movie was a Cadillac with no engine inside, I liked to rewatch it over and over again in every Halloween! But of course “Shining” is one of the masterpieces of MY KING and one of the ten best book of him. (Salem’s Lot and Dead Zone will be always my favorites!)<br /><br />And now the story returns back to inform us what happened to the three survivors of Overlook Hotel. Danny Torrance, his mother Wendy and Dick Halloran. We see older Danny suffers from alcoholism (like father like son, he is about to turn into a dull boy, too!)<br /><br />This book is about Danny’s facing to his own devils and past traumatic experiences. Danny burned the bridges help him reach to his childhood and dug the ashes to the deep. But right now the past demons erupted out to threaten his future. So he has to go to the place where this nightmare begins!<br /><br />His AA group helps him earn his second chance from the life. When he hits the rock bottom, we learn more about the secret he keeps eat him alive. He still has his shining but as his path crosses with the gifted girl whose life in danger by summoning from a group of dangerous psychic vampires, he is adamant to fight back.<br /><br /> Rose the Hat a.k.a Cokehead or once upon a time Irish Rose from Northern Ireland is the leader of the vampire gang. This disturbing, thrilling, awkward as hell group member give you enough creeps to close the book and surf around the comedy channels to recover from too much pressure and stress the book puts you in.<br /><br /> As a matter of fact, I had some second thoughts when I heard my KING wrote the sequel after all those years later. I always wish a happy ending for Danny Boy but I know after all those traumatic experiences they’ve endured with his mother, it might have been impossible for them to live a regular and undamaged, normal life. They had too many invisible emotional scars to achieve that!<br />But I loved the last conclusion, having another journey to the Overlook and villains of the book are perfectly developed to give you good nightmares.<br /><br />LET’S HAIL TO THE KING! APPLAUSE HIM! He is one of the greatest authors of the century and he did it again. I never get disappointed after reading a long KING book. I still use some of them as weights to strengthen my arms. So mentally and psychically his books always help me a lot!!!</span>

<div id="review_2133538860" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2133538860" />
    <a title="Lyn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5253785-lyn"><img alt="Lyn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1495541962p2/5253785.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2133538860?book_show_action=true">Sep 30, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lyn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lyn" href="/user/show/5253785-lyn">Lyn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2133538860" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1514615795871536148">A very good Stephen King book.<br/><br/>I went to see a concert last year featuring Joan Jett, Cheap Trick and Heart. Promoters called it the Hall of Fame tour because all three bands were in the Rock and Roll Hall of Fame. It was a great show, we had a blast. I got the impression that any of these talented professionals could put on a great show in their sleep. They’ve been doing it so long that they knew their craft as well as how to win over a crowd.<br/><br/>Stephen King is also a wily old master craftsman who </span>
  <span id="freeText1514615795871536148" style="display:none">A very good Stephen King book.<br><br>I went to see a concert last year featuring Joan Jett, Cheap Trick and Heart. Promoters called it the Hall of Fame tour because all three bands were in the Rock and Roll Hall of Fame. It was a great show, we had a blast. I got the impression that any of these talented professionals could put on a great show in their sleep. They’ve been doing it so long that they knew their craft as well as how to win over a crowd.<br><br>Stephen King is also a wily old master craftsman who knows how to grab a reader and hold him entranced for hundreds of pages. Hell, he’s practically a genre unto himself now, leaving behind the Horror and Fantasy schools for a stage just for him. And while I would agree that he, like Joan Jett and Ann Wilson, could put on a great show without trying very hard, I think he did put some extra effort into Doctor Sleep, his 2013 sequel to his 1980 masterpiece <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11588.The_Shining__The_Shining___1_" title="The Shining (The Shining, #1) by Stephen King" rel="nofollow noopener">The Shining</a>.<br><br>While this takes off from where The Shining left off and then goes on to tell its own story, this is in many ways an amalgam of many of his best stories and returns to many of the themes that have made him one of our most successful writers. I noticed elements of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/33124137.Pet_Sematary" title="Pet Sematary by Stephen King" rel="nofollow noopener">Pet Sematary</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/233667.Firestarter" title="Firestarter by Stephen King" rel="nofollow noopener">Firestarter</a>, and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11573.The_Dead_Zone" title="The Dead Zone by Stephen King" rel="nofollow noopener">The Dead Zone</a>. Besides trying to scare the heeby-jeebies out of us, King explores themes of family, life and death, extra sensory perceptions, and the demons that haunt us, paranormal and mundane.<br><br>King, a recovering alcoholic, wrote The Shining as an alcoholic and Doctor Sleep speaks from this mature, embattled perspective. Sadly, but fittingly, little Danny Torrance becomes too much like his father and has succumbed to his inherited drinking problem. King shares with us, no doubt from much of his own experience, how Alcoholics Anonymous helps Dan Torrance survive and thrive in sobriety, but also shares Dan’s rock bottom and how this hidden secret gnaws at Torrance as much as the ghosts from the Overlook Hotel. In this way, King provides an allegory for secrets held and like so much of his writing, finds the horrific without delving too far into fantasy. We are our own worst enemies – and nightmares.<br><br>Years after the tragedy at the Overlook, Dan Torrance is making his way from childhood to alcoholic despondency to an edgy and fragile temperance. Like most recovering alcoholics, he takes his life one step at a time, and one day at a time. And his gift of shining remains. Using his special abilities to help dying patients in a hospice, he has come to the sobriquet of Doctor Sleep. It is here that Dan discovers a young girl who makes his shining look dim by comparison; as his is a flashlight, hers is a light house. Dan also discovers an antagonistic group who feed on human suffering, and the suffering of those with the shining is their most cherished delicacy.<br><br>Rose the Hat. Leading this group of psychic vampires is one of King’s most devilish and engaging characters. From Northern Ireland (centuries ago – drawing on the vampire parallel) Rose was once Irish Rose, but now in her leadership role, she is Rose the Hat, appearing with a cocked to one side old top hat. King has made a good living on making bad guys scary and evil and in Rose he has given us one of his most dire, giving old Barlow a run for his money.<br><br>So I raise my lighter to you, Mr. King, great show.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1570727053i/28274157._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="209" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="1514615795871536148" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_695125372" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/695125372" />
    <a title="Dan Schwent" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/870755-dan-schwent"><img alt="Dan Schwent" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1593973948p2/870755.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/695125372?book_show_action=true">Aug 14, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dan Schwent" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dan Schwent" href="/user/show/870755-dan-schwent">Dan Schwent</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/870755-dan-schwent?shelf=2013">2013</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer695125372&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer695125372" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11063767709836551197">Dan Torrance grew up to be an alcoholic, just like his father. But now he's in recovery and working in a hospice where he uses his Shine to comfort people when they die. But what is his connection to a young girl named Abra Stone? And what does The True Knot, a traveling group of RV people, want with her?<br/><br/>After all the glimpses shown in <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15729539.NOS4A2' title='NOS4A2 by Joe Hill' rel='nofollow noopener'>NOS4A2</a>, I knew I'd be reading this one hot off the presses. Was I disappointed? Well, I don't think it was a home run.<br/><br/>I loved the story of Dan Torrance, recoverin</span>
  <span id="freeText11063767709836551197" style="display:none">Dan Torrance grew up to be an alcoholic, just like his father. But now he's in recovery and working in a hospice where he uses his Shine to comfort people when they die. But what is his connection to a young girl named Abra Stone? And what does The True Knot, a traveling group of RV people, want with her?<br /><br />After all the glimpses shown in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15729539.NOS4A2" title="NOS4A2 by Joe Hill" rel="nofollow noopener">NOS4A2</a>, I knew I'd be reading this one hot off the presses. Was I disappointed? Well, I don't think it was a home run.<br /><br />I loved the story of Dan Torrance, recovering from his experience at the Overlook with his parents in <br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11588.The_Shining__The_Shining___1_" title="The Shining (The Shining, #1) by Stephen King" rel="nofollow noopener">The Shining</a>, only to become an alcoholic just like his old man. His road to recovery was well done and I loved how the connection to Abra Stone unfolded. Dan's friends were well done and I found myself dreading which one of them would die at the bloody conclusion, as is the fate of many Stephen King supporting cast members.<br /><br />There were some nice Easter eggs in Doctor Sleep. Charles Manx, Castle Rock, the Dark Tower, and probably a few others I've already forgotten. When Dan got a job at TeenyTown, I had flashbacks of Joyland. Maybe Joyland started life as a fragment of Doctor Sleep that got cut out like a bad appendix. Also, I have a feeling Stephen King read a book about carnies and felt the need to work as much lingo into his work as possible.<br /><br />Another thing I loved was the True Knot. I love the idea of a bunch of psychic vampires riding around in RVs, draining kids of their Shine to rejuvenate them. Rosie the Hat was pretty vile and her compatriots were almost as bad. I almost feared for Abra Stone's life.<br /><br />Almost. My main problem with the book is that Abra was too damn powerful and I never thought for a moment that she wouldn't survive. When she outmaneuvers the bad guys at every turn, there's no sense of jeopardy. The ending was straight from the Nerf factory. I don't remember another Stephen King book where so many of the good guys survived the final encounter.<br /><br />Still, it was a fun read and there were some tense moments. We'll call it a 3.5.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11063767709836551197" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2253416286" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2253416286" />
    <a title="Annemarie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27544490-annemarie"><img alt="Annemarie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1593255949p2/27544490.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2253416286?book_show_action=true">Jan 11, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Annemarie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Annemarie" href="/user/show/27544490-annemarie">Annemarie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="paperback 9781529375060" href="/book/show/52670079-doctor-sleep-film-tie-in">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27544490-annemarie?shelf=read-in-german">read-in-german</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27544490-annemarie?shelf=read-in-english">read-in-english</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2253416286" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11381934585086405324"><b>Actual rating: 4.50 🌟 </b><br/><br/>This was a great book that was much more than a simple sequel. It's a book with its own story and doesn't just depend on the fame of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11588.The_Shining__The_Shining___1_' title='The Shining (The Shining, #1) by Stephen King' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Shining</a>. Of course there are references, and reading the first book before this one will help you understand the content much better, but it's clear that this book wasn't just written for the sole purpose of making more money and drawing out a story to an unnecessary length (like I have seen done before)- I would love to read more sequels </span>
  <span id="freeText11381934585086405324" style="display:none"><b>Actual rating: 4.50 🌟 </b><br /><br />This was a great book that was much more than a simple sequel. It's a book with its own story and doesn't just depend on the fame of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11588.The_Shining__The_Shining___1_" title="The Shining (The Shining, #1) by Stephen King" rel="nofollow noopener">The Shining</a>. Of course there are references, and reading the first book before this one will help you understand the content much better, but it's clear that this book wasn't just written for the sole purpose of making more money and drawing out a story to an unnecessary length (like I have seen done before)- I would love to read more sequels of this kind!<br /><br />Like in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11588.The_Shining__The_Shining___1_" title="The Shining (The Shining, #1) by Stephen King" rel="nofollow noopener">The Shining</a>, you will find several points of view. This was very well done, despite how different the characters were from each other. Everyone has their own distinctive voice, which does deserve a mention as the two main characters have a huge age difference and I'm sure not every author would have been able to develop such fitting personalities for both of them.<br /><br />I love that we get an insight into the life of the characters spanning several years before the prime storyline begins. This really helps painting a clear picture of everyone, and I was able to understand Dan Torrance better than I might would have without this leadup.<br /><br />It was really great to get a more diverse and evolved look at what the gift of "The Shining" is and what it all entails. All in all it was just very interesting and at this point I totally wouldn't be surprised if someone came up to me and told me that they have experienced the same things the people in the book have. Stephen King just has this way of writing that makes everything seem real and believable.<br /><br />There's a huge banger late in the book that totally surprised me! But again, it was done in a believable way and didn't totally seem unsuitable. Looking back at it, little hints were being carefully and nicely placed throughout the book.<br /><br />I thought the resolution to everything was just perfect. It was done realistically (as realistic as it can get with a plot like this) and not over the top. I was even tearing up a bit at a certain scene, which I thought was just a perfect addition to connect the previous book to this one.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11381934585086405324" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer683510511" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer17180004757814138769">I hesitated to read DOCTOR SLEEP for about a minute. I was worried that it wouldn't live up to The Shining, and everything would be ruined. RUINED! <br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1383378884i/6528857.jpg' alt=' photo 29b07314-4401-4a70-bc94-0c1a75fe7104_zps6c5aafda.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Luckily that was not the case at all. I should have had more faith in Stephen King's love and respect for these characters. I am sorry for ever doubting you Stephen.<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1383371498i/6526797.jpg' alt=' photo d5d105f4-017f-42ee-9eb7-5cc0830df130_zpsac9826ba.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>A tribe of people called The True Knot travel around the United States- by RV- in search of children with "The Shining". These children have what The True Knot feeds off, something they c</span>
  <span id="freeText17180004757814138769" style="display:none">I hesitated to read DOCTOR SLEEP for about a minute. I was worried that it wouldn't live up to The Shining, and everything would be ruined. RUINED! <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1383378884i/6528857.jpg" alt=" photo 29b07314-4401-4a70-bc94-0c1a75fe7104_zps6c5aafda.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Luckily that was not the case at all. I should have had more faith in Stephen King's love and respect for these characters. I am sorry for ever doubting you Stephen.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1383371498i/6526797.jpg" alt=" photo d5d105f4-017f-42ee-9eb7-5cc0830df130_zpsac9826ba.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>A tribe of people called The True Knot travel around the United States- by RV- in search of children with "The Shining". These children have what The True Knot feeds off, something they call "steam". Their leader- Rose "The Hat" learns of a little girl -named Abra- that will keep them in steam for a very long time.<br><br>Danny Torrance is all grown up, but far from happy. He is still haunted by his past. To numb the pain, and keep the ghosts at bay, he follows in his fathers footsteps with the bottle. Dan finally settles down in a little town in New Hampshire , joins AA, and finds a little bit of peace...until one day he starts receiving strange telepathic messages from a little girl named Abra. Abra needs his help.<br><br>Call me crazy, but I think I liked DOCTOR SLEEP more than I liked The Shining. I could be terribly wrong because I haven't read The Shining in years, but I certainly loved grown up Danny waaaaaaay more than I liked Jack, and I loved Abra more than I liked Danny as a child. One thing I do know as a fact... I will never look at "innocent" summer vacationers travelling in RVs the same. EVER!<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1383371957i/6526882.jpg" alt=" photo efec1d50-2f82-4e14-a721-ccddf1a79fce_zps739a4985.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>

<div id="review_1671678882" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1671678882" />
    <a title="Johann (jobis89)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/50893023-johann-jobis89"><img alt="Johann (jobis89)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588540681p2/50893023.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1671678882?book_show_action=true">Jun 17, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Johann (jobis89)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Johann (jobis89)" href="/user/show/50893023-johann-jobis89">Johann (jobis89)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1671678882" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer999377097883165365">“There came a time when you realised that moving on was pointless. That you took yourself with you wherever you went.”<br/><br/>A worthy sequel to The Shining, Doctor Sleep revisits Danny Torrance as an adult, where he has unfortunately inherited his father’s alcoholism, but also retains his ability to “shine”. He encounters a young girl named Abra, who needs his help to fight the vampiric cult, the True Knot.<br/><br/>There’s so much I love about this book that I almost don’t know where to begin! The book opens st</span>
  <span id="freeText999377097883165365" style="display:none">“There came a time when you realised that moving on was pointless. That you took yourself with you wherever you went.”<br /><br />A worthy sequel to The Shining, Doctor Sleep revisits Danny Torrance as an adult, where he has unfortunately inherited his father’s alcoholism, but also retains his ability to “shine”. He encounters a young girl named Abra, who needs his help to fight the vampiric cult, the True Knot.<br /><br />There’s so much I love about this book that I almost don’t know where to begin! The book opens strongly with throwbacks to the ghosts from The Shining, as we follow Danny and Wendy after their stint in the Overlook Hotel. These references to The Shining are scattered throughout the novel and I couldn’t help but revel in each of these moments. Doctor Sleep can easily stand on its own merit, but those little tie-ins truly enhance the experience.<br /><br />It’s heartbreaking to see Dan struggle with the same illness that haunted his father. But I also appreciate that Dan has his own flaws and is not presented as a purely heroic figure. The fantastic characterisation follows with the introduction of Abra - another solid King child character. This girl is an absolute badass. I LOVE HER.<br /><br />Admittedly the True Knot aren’t my favourite villains... I think Rose the Hat is brilliant, but a lot of the others became interchangeable for me. Although I wouldn’t even classify this one as being scary, some parts were pretty unnerving. The baseball boy parts in particular cut me up, they’re brutal.<br /><br />Incase it isn’t obvious, I truly loved this one just as much on my reread. I just loved getting to revisit Dan Torrance as an adult and he feels so true to young Danny. Even though this one is a relatively recent King, the writing style etc did feel more akin to old King for me!<br /><br />Love, love, love! 5 stars.</span>
  <a data-text-id="999377097883165365" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_377104034" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/377104034" />
    <a title="Matt" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5903843-matt"><img alt="Matt" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603562140p2/5903843.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/377104034?book_show_action=true">Jul 25, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Matt" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Matt" href="/user/show/5903843-matt">Matt</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audiobook 9781442357617" href="/book/show/15800595-doctor-sleep">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5903843-matt?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer377104034" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12408350055864212733">Stephen King’s title of ‘great storyteller’ is firmly strengthened with this full-length novel, which reprises some of the key roles from The Shining. Picking up briefly after THE SHINING’s completion, Danny Torrance and his mom have moved on, away from the horrors of Colorado. Learning to control his ‘shines’ proves to be quite difficult for Danny, but becomes essential in order to survive. Fast-forwarding to the present day, Dan Torrance’s life has begun to circle the drain as he has become a </span>
  <span id="freeText12408350055864212733" style="display:none">Stephen King’s title of ‘great storyteller’ is firmly strengthened with this full-length novel, which reprises some of the key roles from The Shining. Picking up briefly after THE SHINING’s completion, Danny Torrance and his mom have moved on, away from the horrors of Colorado. Learning to control his ‘shines’ proves to be quite difficult for Danny, but becomes essential in order to survive. Fast-forwarding to the present day, Dan Torrance’s life has begun to circle the drain as he has become a replica of his alcoholic father. Struggling to survive, Dan drifts from town to town, eventually settling in New Hampshire, where he’s given a second chance, with a fast-track path to AA. While he gets his life together, a baby, Abra Stone, begins to show signs of the shine, though no one knows what to make of her premonitions. Her family is unaware of these shines, chalking them up to coincidence or unexplained circumstances. Meanwhile, a sinister group of people, the TRUE KNOT begin leeching the life out of people wherever they go, using their ‘steam’ to survive. Children with the shine are the Knot’s favourite snack and keeps them surviving for decades. When their leader connects with Abra and her abilities, all paths lead to finding her and destroying this uber-shiner. When Abra reaches out to fellow shiner, Dan, they connect and realise just how horrific the Knots can be and how much trouble surrounds them. While Dan and Abra fight to hide from the Knot and destroy them at the same time, the story kicks into high gear and its pace is non-stop, leaving the reader to grip onto anything they can as they fly through this action-packed sequel.<br /><br />King’s powerful return to his Shining roots proves not only useful but highly worthwhile. As King denotes in his author’s note, many people have wondered whatever happened to little Danny Torrance and if there is more to The Shining than meets the eye (or brainwave). King layers old Shining memories with new ideas and powerful characters, while kicking the horror genre up a notch. Filled with his linguistic nuances and apt off-the-beaten-path comments, King uses this unique style to cater to his long-time fans’ interest in his style. There are few authors who can scare a reader so soundly and yet keep them begging for more, while also telling a multi-layered novel with a foundation so sound that it cannot collapse on itself.<br /><br />Kudos Mr. King. While I used to think you the devil-incarnate (blame my upbringing), I can now say you are one of the great fiction writers of my time.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12408350055864212733" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_727990642" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/727990642" />
    <a title="D. Hilliard" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4133821-d-hilliard"><img alt="D. Hilliard" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1347766874p2/4133821.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/727990642?book_show_action=true">Sep 25, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="D. Hilliard" class="user" itemprop="url" name="D. Hilliard" href="/user/show/4133821-d-hilliard">D. Hilliard</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/17406532-doctor-sleep">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer727990642" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4377414076114495252">Being a big fan of Stephen King, especially his early work, I waited with nervous anticipation for Dr. Sleep. I reread The Shining for the first time in years, just to reacquaint myself with the world of Danny Torrance and the Overlook Hotel. It was on my kindle within minutes of it being released, and I spent the past two afternoons ignoring housework in favor of diving into one of Kings rare sequels.<br/><br/>So how does it measure up?<br/><br/>The correct answer to that is “it depends.”<br/><br/>If you are looking for a d</span>
  <span id="freeText4377414076114495252" style="display:none">Being a big fan of Stephen King, especially his early work, I waited with nervous anticipation for Dr. Sleep. I reread The Shining for the first time in years, just to reacquaint myself with the world of Danny Torrance and the Overlook Hotel. It was on my kindle within minutes of it being released, and I spent the past two afternoons ignoring housework in favor of diving into one of Kings rare sequels.<br /><br />So how does it measure up?<br /><br />The correct answer to that is “it depends.”<br /><br />If you are looking for a direct sequel to The Shining that recaptures the same sense of claustrophobic terror as the original, you are going to be disappointed. It does try to go for scares here and there, but on that level it comes nowhere close to it’s predecessor. If, on the other hand, you are looking for the next story in the life of Danny Torrance then you will probably find this much more satisfying.<br /><br />Dan Torrance is a grown man and an alcoholic who has hit rock bottom and is now trying to recover. He works at a hospice where he uses his talent to help dying patients pass over. Over time he becomes aware of another child with The Shining, and this girl is far more powerful than he was. But there is a group of “psychic vampires” roaming the country and feeding on children who shine, and he is going to get drawn into defending her against these monsters.<br /><br />Sadly, I think the monsters are one of the areas where this book falls short of what it could have been. They simply aren’t very frightening, and the one scene where they kidnap a boy to devour feels tacked on as if the author was trying to make them scarier while introducing a plot device for later. The problem here is that the author spends too much time in the heads of his bad guys. <br /><br />King is a master of characterization, and that shows with many of the characters in this book. You feel real sympathy for Dan Torrance, and connect with several of the other characters as well. At the same time though, he seems to have let that lead him to actually overdevelop some of the bad guys to the point they are merely antagonists, and just don’t inspire fear at all. Rose the Hat is no Walking Dude. Heck, despite her powers she isn’t even as scary as Jack Torrance was.<br /><br />But that is really the only flaw of the book. So the effect of it is, that as a horror book it’s not all that effective, but as a layered story with interesting characters possessing psychic powers, it succeeds in all kinds of ways. I absolutely do recommend this book, but just take it on its own merits.<br /><br />I give it four stars.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="4377414076114495252" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
